Let me give praises to Mike for solving my CEL (check engine light) problem. My OBD computer gave me P0174 & P0330, faulty O2 sensor & knock sensors replacement. Mike's Auto also came up with same computer diagnostic readings.

I replaced 2 of 3 O2 sensors myself. The third sensor was seized, which I couldn't remove with my tools & lubricating spray. Toyota of HB wanted to replace the entire exhaust manifold. That was unacceptable with a $2000 quote. Mike's auto has the knowledge & tools to remove the seized sensor, thus saving me $2K. I supplied the sensor & paid a fair labor charge.

I already knew the knock sensors replacement would be the expensive part b/c it is labor-intensive. Based on what I researched, Mike's quote was fair. Based on what I've read on Yelp & on the company's website, I felt comfortable giving them my business.

I waited almost 3 weeks to write this review to make sure that my 2002 Toyota Highlander was running fine, & it is. It has 185K miles, & I would like it to last 300K & beyond, if possible. I also have a 1998 Toyota Camry with 250K miles & will bring it to Mike's for 255K service.< /review>

< review>
Due to the sheer volume of fake 5 star reviews, the highest grade I ever give the best service is 4 stars.

Visiting a vet rates on the list of preferred activities just below getting a root canal.   I hate how many vets leverage your predicament to their financial gain.   To my amazement, after visiting many clinics over the years, this clinic restored my faith in humanity.  The cost was never mentioned until we were ready to leave, and was so low I felt a tad guilty as if I cheated them.  The receptionist did mention half price of normal cost for first visit, but even if the cost for visit, after deducting cost of medicine, it still would have been a bargain, even compared to those so called "discount" clinics, none of which I will identify by name.  To summarize, we didn't feel as if we were haggling over the purchase price of car, what a relief.

Another interesting theme with this business is the women, and I will not mention her name due to the fact that most reviews praising individuals by name were left by that person, the tall women really and truly loves cats.   She mentioned having 5 herself.   You can see a marked difference in the cat's willingness to cooperate, especially given the vet's patience, sympathy, and knowledge.  The woman really was a champ.   I'm not looking forward to a returning visit, but if I do suddenly need to take my cat to the vet, this place is certainly my choice of preference.

There you have my two cents, take it for what it's worth.<//review>

< Text>
This vet clinic is awesome!  I researched various vets in the area, and it had fabulous reviews, so I went to check it out.  My cat had a scratched eye.  As a new client, I got 50% my first office visit.  The clinic isn't a large office, but you get great care with reasonable prices!  The office was exceptionally clean and didn't have the usual vet odor. The vet took her time with Misty, explained her injury, and informed me about everything before conducting any additional testing, which would be my choice. She left with some eye drops and a conehead, but her eye was healed within a week.  The vet even called me during the week to see how she was doing.  I went for a week check-up to make sure she had healed okay.  The vet also called again that week to make sure she was well.  I highly recommend you visit the North Tustin Veterinary Clinic. < Text>
I've been going to Yuki for over 10 years now (they didn't start at this location).  The food has always been awesome, hands down the best fresh sushi (read nigiri and sashimi)  I've had in this area or pretty much anywhere else for that matter.

Where they fall short is on the service side.  They're very busy and the waiters are always rushing back and forth but you usually have to ask to get your tea refilled and orders frequently don't arrive at the same time (or even close together).

I'm a die hard fan of the food though and will continue to go but I do wish they'd hire more help for the floor, even if it's temp to get through the busy periods.<//Text>

< review>
One of the best places to go to for fresh anything really :) I love going here for their sushi, combinations, and udon!

They're only open from Tuesday to Saturday, they close Monday and Sunday. I would always recommend getting their sushi because it's really fresh! The restaurant is authentic japanese and they really care about the quality of their fish which is why the food here is delicious.

Some of my favorite dishes are:

Nabeyaki Udon: The flavor of their broth is amazing. It's sweet but savory and there is just a ton of flavor. The Udon size is small but they pack it with a lot of stuff! The noodles were nice and chewy and I also like the tempura that comes with it because I think they make really good tempura!

Grilled Mackerel/Saba: They make really tasty fish. They grill and smoke the fish so you can taste that smoky flavor which makes their fish so delicious.

Ginger Beef: This is one of my favorite dishes to get in the dinner or lunch combinations. The beef is really tender and full of flavor. The beef is thinly sliced and sits on top of a sizzling platter!

Sushi: I can't remember all the different sushi i got here but I remember them being really good and fresh.

They always have daily specials on the white board near the sushi bar so look out of those because there always some really good things on there! The wait can get pretty long because there isn't too many seating but it's cute small restaurant.</review>

< UserId.>
113812994344388633166</UserId.>
< name>
Clarissa Ryan</name>
<date>1357932157554<//date><rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Yuki is one of only a couple of authentic, Japanese-Japanese restaurants in Fremont. It often gets low marks on certain review sites because people go in expecting Crazy Super Gonzo Rolls and they throw a fit when they don't get them. Well, too bad. It's not that kind of place. Here you will find Japanese home-cooking-style dishes (nabe, croquettes, etc.), basic but good sushi (nigiri and maki), basic but good sashimi, a very short selection of California-style sushi rolls, and a handful of unfussy fusion items because, as the Japanese friend who introduced it to us said, "the chef likes to experiment." Their Cali-style items are actually pretty good; they smoke their own salmon, as I recall, so the smoked salmon and cream cheese roll is unreasonably delicious. Their mackerel is excellent and it's the first place I ever really liked it. Ramen is not a specialty, though; I would get that somewhere else.

Service can be slow. Prices are fair; combination meals are pretty large.

Adjust your expectations and you will have the best Japanese eating experience in Fremont. If all you want is multi-colored rolls with lots of sauces, though--and I admit those can be tasty--please go somewhere else.</Review>

<Review>I first came to Dr Kim in Jan 2017 and needed to be re-treated for three root canals I'd had done nearly three decades ago, elsewhere. All three re-treatments were done perfectly on my bottom, front teeth. Since I had three crowns on them, he told me I could lose all three, but I only lost one that had a post. It takes a very-skilled surgeon to accomplish that. Nearly three years later, they became a problem again. Dr. Kim had warned me about this, and I had also read about the odds of root canals becoming re-infected. This time, he did not recommend re-treating, but thought I should get a bridge. I had that done at Folsom Hills dentistry, Dr. O'Donnell, where I've gone  since 2014, and it worked out very well. I have Delta Dental insurance, and their yearly plans start at around $90 a year, for singles, and then they pay half of everything covered, plus a small office charge each time you go. For the bridge work, the dental office told me about Comenity - Smile Generation Financial. If you're approved, the office does the paperwork, and my half of the bill, after insurance, was $2258. The great part is that I have two years to pay it with no interest. For those of us who don't have work-related dental insurance, Delta Dental HMO insurance is a wonderful plan. They have a PPO plan too, but you have to wait a year before getting certain services covered. Go see Dr. Kim - he's one of the best, as is his office staff.<//Review><userid>114718457328239433960</userid>< Pics>

< review>
I feel like a kid going to this store. They serve varieties of fun, quirky products like wasabi toothpaste or buffalo wings flavored soda. Yes, you read that correctly.

Aside from that, they also sell craft soda and root beers, among variety of candies that you don't usually find in your usual mini markets.

I ended up getting a few bottles of craft root beers (delicious!), a bottle of peanut butter soda (horrible!), and a tube of wasabi tooth paste (too scared to try..).

Overall, a good experience, and I'll definitely come back again whenever I need my craft root beer fix, or if I'm feeling adventurous :)< /review>
